< text>
Beautiful facility with ballrooms and main theatre. Nice grounds with kids play area and there is a parking garage across the street. They have a green room for performers to relax in. I went to the Apple store because my fan sounded off and found out I also had liquid spillage that would have cost me the same amount of getting a brand new Macbook Pro (because they would have to replace every part and I don't have AppleCare) so the Apple tech recommended that I try M.A.C Berkeley in case it might be more cost-effective. <Rate>5< /Rate>< review>
Often when you go to a new age restaurant, the new is often a mix of things, in the name of new age 'whatever' cuisine and more often than not it just does not work together. When it does, you get the Hokkaido Scallops, which goes off in your mouth with explosive citrus flavors nicely balanced  that it doesn't overpower but complement the scallops nicely.

If you think that's the best you can get at a "new age" restaurant, you would be wrong, and for me that moment was when I had the first bite of the Shrimp toast. Only one word to describe it...."Home"! In one meal two dishes had me weak kneed and struggling for words when Ben who was waiting on me asked how it was.

Nightshade's team still does not let up, the pastry chef blows away what's left of you with the coconut mousse, which is a treat to the eye but an even better treat for what makes us feel good! Easily one of the best pastry chef I have ever encountered!

The oysters were interesting but the other 3 were such knockouts and that's what I'll be going back for again!

The cocktail was stunningly refreshing as well. What a treat today was ! ü§ô</review>

< review>
Kusshi oysters were amazing. Clean flavor complimented by passionfruit, and bursts of garlic when downing the leche de tigre. One of my fav courses of the night.

Beef tartare and chicharron are well worth it. With a dash of sesame oil and Korean gochukaru red pepper, the flavors mesh together well and the plate disappeared quite quickly.

Def try the squid ink tagliatelle with cuttlefish. It was very good and the freshly made pasta was delightful. The Bolognese and Korean gochujang or red bean paste compliment one another to produce a flavorful sauce with the cuttlefish.

One item not on the menu was a shrimp and ravioli dish, with a broth made from boiled lobster head and other items. It was delicious. If they are serving it and you like seafood, you absolutely must try it. The ravioli pasta was freshly made and tasted exquisite.

The last item we tried was the pork schnitzel. The pork cutlet (similar to katsu) left a bit to be desired.  I felt like it lacked some spice and was a bit bland. Perhaps it was intentional to let the gwaimei (meaning strange flavor or ugly beauty, something oxymoronic) dressing blossom and take the stage with its vinaigrette-like sweet but sour flavor accompanied by oh-so-delicious green jade tomatoes. I feel like the tomatoes and gwaimei dressing could have been a vegetable dish on it's own. Nonetheless, if you're with a big group though, it's a good dish to order as it is filling for the price.

Last but not least, we finished off with the coconut mousse and was not disappointed. The coconut lime granita provided the perfect citrus kick for the smooth, sweet mousse interior, with a delicious pineapple center.  Nata de coco (aka coconut gel from your typical boba shop) adorns the dish rounding off the delectable dessert.

For drinks we had no. 7 which was fantastic and would cater to anyone with a palette for an old fashioned. No. 923 is sweet but not obnoxious, with an exquisite milk-flavor that's achieved by straining the milk out of the liquid allowing it retain a rich flavor. A must try if you prefer something on the sweeter side.

Overall, an amazing dining experience! Service was impeccable. Kudos to Chef Mei and a fantastic menu. The decor is beautiful too. I will be back to try the rib-eye, scallops, Dungeness crab, quail egg, and guava dessert!< /review>

< Text>
I love open kitchen restaurant spaces, especially when you can sit at the bar and watch them make the food. The ambience, space and service are to notch.

Drinks : Both the old fashioned and the 109 were made perfectly. 100 marks for drinks and presentation.

Food :
Bit of a hit and miss here.
The best dishes we had were the congee and the guava pudding. Both of those were fantabulous.
The congee had just the right amount of sour, salt and a touch of tang to it, while the porridge itself was perfectly prepared.
The guava pudding was very interestingly presented and was a delight in every bite.
The kanpachi was a beautiful presentation again and when blended into the sauce was very flavorful.

The shrimp toast was passable and the hot chicken on Japanese bread was a complete miss. There are much better versions of this dish, it lacked any distinctly Asian flavor.

Ben, our server was a delight, sharp wit and extremely attentive. The only bummer for me was when I walked up to Chef Lin at the end of the night to say thank you she wasn't the least bit interested in interacting and waved us off. I'm sure running a top notch kitchen is stressful so I'll put it down to that, but I was disappointed.

I'd definitely go here if I wanted to make a special evening of it, worth a visit.

Valet was $12 at time of writing.
If the review helped you please click on the üëçüèΩ</Text>

104658089830974681962< /userid>
< text>
It's been a year since the untimely loss of Anthony and Jonathan, who were influential in the LA Food Scene.  In honor of their contributions, I made the trip to Mecca, which would have certainly been on Mr. Gold's 101 list for 2019.  Nightshade is an intriguing name, with thoughts of some nefarious restaurant located in a newly found "Art's District" location.  Finding parking was a good omen, and continued through dinner, as we started with beer and cocktails, moving our way through an appetizer of scallops which melt in your mouth and the infamous Koshihikari Rice Congee, which is so addicting, it aught to be regulated.  We reserved a 25 oz. Short Rib, the smallest they have, and enjoyed the smokey goodness which is very similar to Majordomo's version, but with some nice condiments to go with the butter lettuce wrap.  To seal the deal, we enjoyed a rather healthy dessert of silkened  tofu with baby peaches and chia seeds, which made my stomach feel satiated from the entire dining experience.  I kind of wish I sat at the Chef's table which are simply barstools with a marble tabletop, but a perfect view of the food preparation area.  I hope to come back next week to enjoy the other items on the menu!<//text>

<review>Nightshade was a lovely dining experience on many levels.

Service was fantastic! Not a single complaint. Our server was attentive, kind, offered suggestions and food came out well timed. I can't stand when dishes feel rushed and poorly timed but that was not the case at Nightshade.

The decor and ambience is beautiful. It was smaller than I imagined but you don't feel cramped. The space is minimal and bright.

The menu is creative and relatively diverse. I was a bit surprised there was not a salad option (unless I missed it?). There's a nice mix of seafood, meat and vegetarian options.

I will say, we all were a little stunned by portions. This is a blessing and a curse. I did not leave feeling stuffed, I felt content after my meal but a lot of food was needed for a party of 4 and to be honest, we could have ordered a couple more dishes.

We ordered the following:

1. Scallops- absolutely delicious, I loved the sauce. It had incredible flavor.

2. Oysters- another great option, not a plain oyster. I liked the sauce it was in.

3. Squid ink pasta- has high hopes but wasn't in love. It just lacked flavoring. I found the squid ink pasta and Bestia more exciting.

4. Rice congee- loved this! Definitely one of the more hearty options. Great flavoring and fun to mix up with all the condiments.

5. Shrimp toast- one of my favorites, truly unique and loved the combo of the shrimp and toast and the sauce on the bottom.

6. I loved my cocktail (#914), it had mezcal, tequila, pineapple and black garlic oil. It was light, somewhat sweet and honestly perfect.

Overall, great experience but one time was enough. I'm also not a huge Asian fusion fan so perhaps this just isn't my type of restaurant.< /review>< pics>

<Gmap_id>0x80c2c63ec69d6115:0x1bf821076cfc22d3</Gmap_id><Response>None<//Response>< text>
Nightshade is one of those places that I really wanted to hate on, I am not sure why.  Most likely because I am asian, and I just tend to judge my own people harder --out of love though, because I want them to be better.  It's in the LA arts district where you would expect it to be.  I was assuming the worst - super salty, super annoying staff, and asian fusion in all the wrong ways.  Well, I was pleasantly surprised.  What I found instead was interesting flavors, innovative dishes, and incredibly patient and friendly staff.

Let's start with the hits.  The mapo tofu lasagna is interesting.  It's pretty out there and not something I've ever seen before.  I thought the flavors were good and I would recommend this dish since it was pretty different.
The oysters I also enjoyed, but this one also had different opinions at the table.   I liked the passion fruit flavor and the smokiness, but some of my buddies thought it was a little to smoky.  The beef tartare was on point.  The prawn toast was something we had to stop ourselves short of licking the plate.

I wasn't too impressed with the congee, but that might be because I would expect more from this dish.  It was way too spicy to enjoy any of the flavors.  The squid ink tagliatelle wasn't super special, I probably wouldn't opt to get this again.

The desserts were bomb.  I really enjoyed the silkened tofu, but this is probably more of an acquired taste since some of my buddies thought it was more bland, but I appreciated the light sweetness.

I'm also not usually a fan of guava, but the guava dessert with cream cheese is also a must get.</text>

< Name>
Kell Spark</Name>
<Time>1569507158768</Time><Rate>4<//Rate>< review>
Had to see what all the hype is about, and BF made it happen by planning a surprise date night here. Definitely an ideal date night spot, with the elegant, beautiful interior decor and intimate ambiance. Nightshade is truly a unique and thrilling culinary experience and delight, and definitely worth checking out.

Menu is meant to be enjoyed family style, and we ordered the following to share:

Tom yum blooming onion - unique rendition on the famous blooming onion you may have previously encountered at an Outback restaurant. This one has a deep, unique tom yum flavoring that's prominent yet well balanced, and the onion is crisply deep fried, with the individual layers holding firm and crispy even when pulled apart. The dipping sauce is unique as well, offering a creamy complement to the spiced, fried onion, and a very pretty pale shade of green.

Baja kanpachi - served in a very very large bowl for such a petite portion. There's also some type of flat, paper-like garnish on top of the kanpachi, so the sashimi is not even visible at first. This was fresh and super refreshing, and a delicious way to start the meal, and such a stark yet welcome contrast flavor-profile-wise and texturally to the blooming onion.

Mapo tofu lasagna - again, such a unique rendition of two classic dishes (lasagna and mapo tofu) fused together. The lasagna component comes from the visual (the layers) and the pork ragu, which was thick and hearty and deliciously flavored. The mapo tofu aspect comes from the tofu cream that fills the layers of the "lasagna." It's sprinkled with parmesan on top, which adds a nice, salty extra touch and flavor. This is one of the most unique dishes I've experienced, and it was so rich and creamy and a very exciting comfort food item.

Prawn toast - my favorite item of the night. It's perhaps less impressive in terms of visuals, compared to the other highly visually interesting items, but the taste completely won us over. It's a heavier dish, but well balanced, with so much flavor and textures. The crispy deep fried crust of the toast with the creamy Cantonese curry was the perfect combo, and each bite was heavenly and bursting with flavor.

Tamarind glazed carrots - if carrots tasted like this all the time, I would be eating carrots way more. The carrots are well-seasoned and slightly sweet and the sauce was one of the best concoctions I've ever tasted. The garnishes provided different textures, further elevating this side dish.

Dessert & drinks - don't skip on either! Can't remember the names/specifics, but both our drinks as well as the dessert we shared were unique, extremely well crafted, and we were impressed by all.<//review>

<user>108239533538402374451< /user><user_name>Laura C</user_name><time>1556779230238< /time><Rate>4< /Rate><review>This was a highly anticipated restaurant on my list. I‚Äôve heard so much praise and was so ecstatic to try their menu with some friends!

Here‚Äôs what we ordered:
- Oysters: Kushi oysters served on a half shell with passionfruit cream. The cream brings the tartness down a bit and it pairs very well with the oysters. I enjoyed it very much. Very refreshing!
- Hokkaido Scallops: Great presentation but small portion for $23... its essentially 3 scallops sliced to thinner pieces. They drizzle a coconut vinaigrette and it‚Äôs topped with crispy ginger, green chili, pickled shallot, and red coriander. I would‚Äôve preferred a lighter sauce that‚Äôs not cream based but the shallot and red coriander added a nice touch but not memorable.
- Baja Kanpachi: Oh man... 3 slices of amberjack resting on the side of a large bowl, hidden under slices of radishes and a perilla leaf. We were asked to dip the fish into the turnip soup. It has a mild citrus taste. Good but not impressed.
- Squid ink tagliatelle: I love that they used handmade pasta. They‚Äôve added chunks of cuttlefish in the bolognese and mixed in gochujang for a sweet and subtle kick! The pasta was thin and absorbed the sauce nicely!
- Lasagna: This is honestly a brilliant idea! Using bean curd skin as the pasta sheets, each layer is topped with pork ragu and tofu cream. The flavors were a play on the classic Chinese dish ‚ÄúMapo Tofu‚Äù. The edges crisp up so delicately and the texture was amazing! However, as a Chinese home cook, I‚Äôm baffled by how much they charge for such a thin slice, when the ingredient are so cheap! Had they picked a more reasonable price point for a so called lasagna... I wouldn‚Äôt have any complaints. This was also heavily salted.
- Shrimp toast: I didn‚Äôt except this dish to be served as a fried shrimp paste. It sits over a toast in a creamy coconut curry. I loved the flavor and execution. I think what bothered me was how shrimp paste is associated with cheap street food. It‚Äôs also hard to mess up.
- Szechuan hot quail: This is a clever twist by using Szechuan peppers for a shot at Nashville hot chicken. This dish totally took me by surprise. Quail is typically served like a mini roast duck. It‚Äôs all dark meat. I‚Äôm slightly disappointed that it‚Äôs deep fried so you can‚Äôt taste the natural flavors of the quail. But the spices were a hit and most of the quail has been deboned! If you love spicy with a little numbness, this is highly recommended!
- Coconuts mousse: The dessert consists of what looks like a craquelin crusted shell with coconut mousse and pineapple chunks. It‚Äôs served over coconut jelly and lime coconut shaved ice. It taste very tropical and fun to eat!
- Guava cheese cream: Our second dessert taste like a creamy sorbet. It‚Äôs made from fresh pink guava and covered with marbles almond flavored white chocolate. The flavors didn‚Äôt mix well but was good individually.

Overall, I enjoyed the meal! The service was excellent! It was eye opening to try some of the creations. However, I didn‚Äôt find some of the price fitted for what was being served. I skipped a lot of the dishes because the ingredients were incredibly  cheap like blooming onion or congee. I wanted to give this 3 stars based on that but it‚Äôs definitely better than average. I do look forward to what they will bring in the next season. Maybe I‚Äôll be back.<//review>< pics>

Byron Yoshida</name>
< text>
Wow, what can I say?! Chef Mei Lin has not skimped on anything here. I would rate Nightshade in the top 5% of restaurants that I‚Äôve visited. The restaurant is well staffed, I think I counted 20+ plus staff. Each person is welcoming and knows their stuff. The atmosphere is romantic with their dim lights, but at the same time lively with their bar being exposed to their open kitchen concept. Chef Mei Lin also chose to use high quality dishes and table ware. All of that is apparent when you visit. No detail is left untouched!
Onto the food‚Ä¶ the menu is simple with 14 dinner items, 3 dessert items and decent listing of spirits, whiskey, scotch, tequila and vodka drinks. The plates are a la carte style so it‚Äôs best to order 5-6+ dishes for 2 people. We had the East Coast Bay Scallops, beef tartare, roasted sunchokes, lasagna, shrimp toast, Szechuan hot quail and coconut mousse for dessert.
-The scallops came out and don‚Äôt even taste or look like scallops! The bitterness of the coriander goes well with the sweetness and sour of the coconut vinaigrette while the crispy ginger goes well with the plumpness of the scallops.
-The texture of the sunchokes is unique and reminds me of a soft baked yam, but with a little more snap. The slight bitterness and sourness of the mole is balanced well with the sweetness of the sunchoke.

-The tar tar is seasoned just right and goes well with the sesame, egg yolk jam and slight spiciness of the kochukaru.
-The shrimp toast is rich, and each bite gives access to the shrimp topping sitting on a slice of Japanese milk bread that‚Äôs been dipped into a nice blend of curry. Very tasty.
-The lasagna is unique and has thin layers of lasagna coupled with bits of pork ragu. The sweetness of the tofu cream and parmesan counters the slight spiciness of the dish.

-Our neighboring guest told us the hot quail was too spicy, but we tried it anyways since we‚Äôre accustomed to Szechuan food. The quail is fried with a nice coating breading and spices. The dish has a kick, so I don‚Äôt recommend it for those that are sensitive to spicy food. The bread helps with keep your taste buds on check and the pickles counter the spicy well with sweet and sour.
-To end our experience, we chose the coconut mousse. Man, this dessert is beautiful and is just filled with so many complimentary and unique flavors. You have the mousse which reminds me of chilled whipped cream, there‚Äôs the sweet and unique texture of nata de coco, the sweet and tart from the bits of coconut hidden in the center all being brought together with the tartness of the coconut lime granita.

I assume the menus are seasonal, so we‚Äôll try to make sure we continue trying their menus. A must try.

Note: Street parking is limited so expect to use valet service.</text>
